This is EXTREMELY easy and very good. It was a little rich. After reading everyone's reviews this is what I did: 4oz of LF cream cheese, 3/4 jar of salsa, 1 small can green chilis. Also, I was running REALLY late so I used the pre-cooked perdue chicken short cuts and they worked perfectly. You can make this ahead, roll and refrigerate until later.

This was delicious! I made it for a Mexican-themed party, everyone loved it! Since I was making it for a large crowd, I marinated 6 chicken breasts in a store bought Fajita marinade and then cooked it on the grill...before cutting it up. Also added twice as much salsa than called for and a can of Mexican corn. Topped it with Monterey Jack cheese and Jalapeno peppers. Served it with Mexican Rice, chopped lettuce & tomato, and sour cream. Yum!

These were very good.  I substituted reduced fat cream cheese and corn tortillas.  Those parts of the tortillas that weren't covered with cheese turned hard.  Next time, I'll poor a can of enchilada sauce over the top (but under the cheese), both the alleviate the hard spots and because I think it will taste even better.  I served these with chopped lettuce and tomatoes, taco sauce and sour cream.  Also, this made either 10 or 11 enchiladas which I was able to squeeze into a 9x13 pan quite easily.

text:
A perfect fast & easy recipe that everyone really liked!  I used the quantities of ingredients as written including using the full amount of 8 oz reduced fat cream cheese.  My only addition was to add 1/2 c. frozen corn into the filling for some texture and I'd do that again.  Next time the only change that I see as essential would be to use UNSALTED beans.  The purpose of this recipe is to be easy and it's so good exactly as written that I wouldn't fiddle with it too much.  However, if I had an extra couple minutes, I would add some fresh cilantro on top and some chopped onions and frozen corn inside.  I wouldn't alter the ratio of salsa and cream cheese as some others recommend, as increasing canned salsa just adds more salt...I think some fresh tomatoes would be a better choice if you want more stuff inside.  It's hard to believe that a recipe this simple could be so great, but it is...try it with confidence as written. It is also easy to customize to your preferences with just an extra couple minutes of prep time, but you really don't need to change a thing, just watch the salt.

text:
My fiance and I love to try new recipes, but we have a short list of "go to" recipes that we frequently repeat. These enchiladas will probably be added to that list. They were quick, delicious, and the ingredients are cheap. We cooked our chicken on the George Foreman with a bit of poultry seasoning, cumin, and chili powder before dicing them up to add to the sauce. Very quick cooking method and it provided some added flavor. 

But if you're some sort of enchilada snob who is looking for an "authentic" enchilada recipe, keep looking. These aren't traditional enchiladas, but for those looking for a yummy Mexican-inspired dish, you will probably enjoy these. By the way, people who drastically alter recipes should not rate them. Ricotta cheese has a completely different flavor (and texture) than cream cheese. No comparison. To use ricotta and then give this recipe a 1 is a bit unfair.

text:
This was sooooooo good. I did do a few things differently, only because I used what I had on hand. I have hungry, hungry boys to feed, so I doubled the recipe, for starters. Instead of salsa, I used large can of rotel. Instead of pinto beans, Iused a can of Ranch style beans, rinsed(essentially pintos) and a can of black beans. Added shredded Monterey Jack.  I used corn tortillas, instead of flour. And the change that I think had the biggest impact, was a used a can o green enchilada sauce. To make this recipes even easier, I made it more like a casserole, and cut the tortillas into quarters, layered the bottom of the dish with two layers of tortillas, then covered them  with enchilada sauce(about half the can.) Next,  I put the mixture to cover the tortillas(Iused all of it.) I like onion, so I sprinkled minced onions over the mixture, as well as some garlic powder.  Add, enough quartered tortillas to cover the mixture and poered the remaining enchilada sauce tocover tortillas. Finally,  I covered with cheese(any cheese will do.)  I have tried literally hundreds of recipes from this site and this recipe just went straight to the Number 1 spot!!! Thank you so much for adding this one!

text:
Good recipe. Like other reviewers I halved the cream cheese and replaced the salsa with enchilada sauce. I mean they are enchiladas, why not use the right sauce. I sweated some onions and then added my cream cheese (onion and chive was all I had on hand) and half the 10oz can of enchilada sauce. Once this was all melded together I added the chicken(3 cups) and half the contents of a small can of diced green chilies, I thought about using diced jalapenos but my wife would not have approved. I then spooned this mixture into six tortillas and arranged them in a casserole dish. The remaining enchilada sauce was then poured over them along with two cups of a Mexican blend shredded cheese and some diced onions, then into the oven they went. This came out awesome, I can't wait for leftover-lunch today!

text:
I love this recipe!  I have been making enchiladas and using this recipe exactly as written for over a year now.  Just yesterday I tried to make it a bit healthier by substituting the cream cheese with greek yogurt.  It tasted great..the only thing is that the yogurt is thinner so the consistency was a bit different.  If you are going to use greek yogurt, use the Chobiani 2% because the 0% will be too thin...even though it's not fat free, the 2% is still way healthier than reduced fat cream cheese.

I followed this recipe pretty much to the letter, though I used "Mexican blend" cheese on top. Hubby told me it's the closest thing to authentic Mexican that he's had in a while, reiterating "Delicious!" while regaling me with tales about "real" Mexican food that he had while based out West. text:
I did not like this recipe as is, but it does have some potential. I changed a couple of things. I did not use the beans or cream cheese. I used a three-cheese mexican blend of cheeses. I cooked the chicken in a frying pan with 1/2 cup salsa, 1/3 cup of chopped onion, and 1/2 cup of the cheese blend. Then, I spooned them into the tortillas as written. In the baking dish (I did not spray; used nonstick), I added 1 cup of salsa, put in the rolled up enchiladas, and topped with more salsa and cheese. I baked uncovered for 20 mins. They were delicious!

text:
I couldn't decide whether to give this 4 stars or 5 because it is not a very gourmet recipe, but, hey, it 's chicken enchiladas for goodness sake! But I had to give it five since it has become my go-to-in-hurry yummy dinner that my whole family likes, even the picky ones. I have made easy ones and more complicated ones and we prefer these. If I'm really throwing them together, I do as written with the addition of enchilada sauce on bottom of pan than across the middle of the top, then the cheese. I LOVE how easy this is! If I have more time, I add fresh cilantro and maybe some green chilis. I have also tried it with corn tortillas, usually flour though because we like just as we'll and I usually have those on hand. In fact, today I had everything on hand except had to use thawed chicken breasts, we prefer the flavor of rotisserie though.Thanks for the recipe! Keeper here.

text:
Delicious!!! A keeper, definitely. Here are some notes: (1) Can add onion for flavor or to stretch meat, (2) Any bean or meat will do, (3) I used corn instead of flour tortillas, (4) I made a casserole rather than rolled-up enchiladas. I added "Red Enchilada Sauce," also from this site, to the top and bottom, and then added the cheese. Delicious!!!!! This is a great recipe for me because I love creamy-style Mexican casseroles but am not crazy about the can of "cream o' chemicals" soup that they invariable include. This way I can have a yummy casserole without all the revolting additives from cream soups. Later note: Being in a hurry, I tried this dish without the added enchilada sauce, and it was still GREAT. So good, in fact, that I think I'll eschew the sauce in the future, just so that I can put it in my "fast and easy" file. One thing I did was to not drain the beans so that there was more liquid to avoid dryness. I also put a layer of sauce on the bottom and on the top. Yum!!

text:
I think this recipe is awesome!! I've made it several times & do something different each time.  For the most part, I use 8 oz cream cheese & a jar of salsa, as I use more chicken than called for (my family loves chicken.)  I use black beans w/jalapenos instead of pinto beans. Like others, I also coat the bottom of the dish with enchilada sauce & use the rest of the Large can to cover the top.  Doing it this way usually ends up making 12 enchiladas because of more meat.  I use 2 baking dishes, a 9 x 13 one (holds 8), and an 8 x 11 one (holds 4). Like I said, these are pretty FAT enchiladas! I, like others, put the cheese on the last 5 minutes.

this is now my "go to" recipe! i cannot say enought good things about this.... we had surprise company while i was prepping it, so i added some extra leftover chicken and steak, (measured to about 2 1/2 cups of chix/steak) as well as using the entire 8 oz. of cream cheese and a total of 2 cups of salsa.... i wanted to stay as close to the original recipe as possible, but i had to wing it with the extra folks to feed. i threw in some hot chili peppers with the salsa/cream cheese mix and it had a very nice warm heat, without being really hot. next time i will put more sauce on the bottom of the pan, though i was begged to "not change a thing!"  made 7 enchiladas, closely wrapped. i used large flour tortilla shells.

I slow cooked '2' chicken breast with cumin and garlic seasoning on them.  Then I shredded the chicken (I like this texture better).  Instead of salsa - I chopped 2 fresh tomatoes, 1 large chopped jalepeno, and some fresh chopped cilantro to the cream cheese mixture.  I rolled them in soft corn tortillas (better flavor than flour - just microvave then first so they are pliable when rolling).  What ever mixture was left over - I put on top of the rolled tortillas.  I then added strips of roasted (peeled) poblano peppers on top. I then lightly spooned on some Enchiladas sauce (bought in the can)on top. For cheese - I used shredded Chihuahua cheese.  Everyone said they were fabulous!  Thanks for this recipe!

text:
Wow, this is the best recipe I have tried for chicken enchiladas so far and the easiest! Tastes so much better than the enchiladas made with canned soup!  You can adjust the calories and heat with the kind of cream cheese and salsa you use.  I used "On the Border" Medium Salsa, and  used chicken from grilled boned chicken breasts. I also used black beans instead of pinto; since that is what I had on hand. I also find it works better for me to use 8" tortillas instead of 6" tortillas.  I didn't have any Colby-Jack cheese for the top, so I used slices of "real medium cheddar" with sliced ripe olives on top.  I did spread a thin layer of Enchilada Sauce on the bottom of the pan and put some on top of the enchiladas before the cheese and olives.  I doubled this recipe (as I always fit 8 tortillas into a 9" x 13" pan. The 4 extras fit nicely into an 8"x8" pan.  This just moved to the top honor of my Chicken Enchilada recipes. Thank you Iankris!!!

text:
I used half the cream cheese, black beans instead of pinto (I really like black beans) and added half a can of green chilies. This was super easy to make and it turned out quite well.  If you top it tightly with aluminum foil the tortillas will remain nice and soft. I baked it for 25 minutes, and then put some cheese on top and baked it uncovered for a few more minutes. They started to get a little hard them. I'm not sure the extra cheese on top really adds anything and would probably leave it off next time but have it on the table as an extra.  Served with extra salsa, sour cream, cheese and green chilies.

text:
I find a few things will help out this recipe and make it the 5 star rating I gave it anyway. Cook chicken in taco seasoning so it has the flavor to start you off (helps give it a little more spice). Then, instead of heating up the salsa and cream cheese, I just smear about a tablespoon of softened, unseasoned cream cheese in a strip on the bottom of each tortilla and then just top it with a tablespoon of Rotel (or salsa and diced green chilis) before adding the chicken and the flavors meld together nicely once baked in the oven. I also prefer to pour enchilada sauce over the top before baking to heighten the flavor. Melts in your mouth!

Very easy and quite delicious. You can make as is or add a few things to make it pop. Either way, just use 1/2 a package of cream cheese. A whole package makes it too rich. I added a small can of green chiles, chopped cilantro and half of a jalapeo pepper for some kick. I also put a light coating of enchilada sauce just to cover the bottom of the baking dish and a small amount on top of the enchiladas before adding the cheese.The flour tortillas are good but the second time I made it I used corn tortillas and it was even that much better!

text:
I put 3 lbs of chicken,1 tsp of garlic powder, 1 teaspoon of onion powder, 2 tsp of chili powder and 2 packets of taco seasoning(1 spicy and 1 mild) in a crock pot and let it cook on high for approximately 3 hours. I shredded the chicken and doubled the cream cheese and salsa. I then followed the recipe adding the chicken and 1 can of pinto beans to the cream cheese and salsa. I put a little Old El Paso Enchilada sauce in my glass dish before placing the enchiladas on top, then I put a little more on top and put Colby Jack on top. I only use corn tortillas. I topped it with a little more salsa and sour cream. Amazing!

Woohoo! These were SO good... this is what I did... had an Old El Paso Enchilada Kit I wanted to get rid of... used the spice packet that came with it when I was cooking the chicken... read the other reviews and didnt want the top of the enchiladas to be hard, so I doubled the sauce (well kinda -  I actually just used the same amount of cream cheese and doubled the salsa) Reserved about 1/3 of this to put on top of the enchiladas, then added the beans and chicken to the other 2/3. Added the reserved sauce to the top, topped with cheese..... DELICIOUS!!  The enchilada spice packet gave it that extra zing some other reviewers thought was missing... I even got to use the enchilada sauce from the kit to make "Best Spanish Rice" on this site... awesome dinner!!

text:
This is super easy and incredibly delicious! This might be one of our favorite dinners now. Here are the modifications we made: 
1. We took others' advice and put half can of red echilada sauce on bottom of pan and the second half on top of the rolled tortillas before we put the cheese on.
2. We added a can of green chiles to the filling.
3. We cooked 3 chicken breasts and while cooking them in the skillet seasoned them with cumin, black pepper, chopped onion, garlic powder, and a little chili powder. 
4. By using the 3 chicken breasts and the recommended 1 package of cream cheese, along with the can of beans (we used black), and salsa we had enough filling for 10 enchiladas. There was a little filling left over that we just smeared in between the rolled enchiladas.
4. We tried to make it a little healthier by using light cream cheese, whole wheat/high fiber tortillas, and 2% shredded Sargento Mexican blend cheese. You couldn't even tell it was light stuff. 
This was a great dinner and we'll definitely make it again. Thanks!!

text:
Four stars because I think it would be too bland without adjustments.

I changed this up a bit, but this is a good, easy baseline recipe. Here is what I did:

Spread a light layer of enchilada sauce over the bottom of a foil-lined 13x9 pan. (Forgot to spray it first with cooking spray and that would have helped after baking.)

In a saucepan, mixed 8 oz of sour cream, a jar of salsa, a 15-oz can of refried beans, and the chicken. Heated enough just to take the chill off the sour cream.

To be more traditional, I used small corn tortillas, and had ample filling to roll enough to fill a complete pan. I then poured the rest of the enchilada sauce on top, then shredded Mexican style cheese (only used about 1-1/4 cups). Baked around 45 mins until the cheese was lightly brown. After plating, topped with a little bit of sour cream, parsley (did not have cilantro), and some left over tomatoes and peppers from the rice recipe below. The enchiladas were DELICIOUS and so easy!

For a side dish, I drained the juice from one can of Rotel canned tomatoes/chilis and added enough water to make two cups. I placed one cup of brown rice in my rice cooker, added the liquid, and about half of the remaining tomatoes/chilis from the can. (Used the other half to top the enchiladas.) This was good, but next time I will use more spices to the rice, like chili powder or cumin.

In the end, a great easy meal with easy cleanup. Thanks for sharing the recipe!

I live in Texas and all enchiladas I've had were made with flour tortillas. I used ground turkey white breast meat and added some taco seasoning to taste. Mixed the meat with cream cheese while a bit warm along with roasted chopped green peppers. I then covered the entire dish in green enchilada sauce and cheese cooked on 325 till bubbly in the middle.about an hour.  No beans for mine.  I freeze the unsauced enchiladas individually then bag them for later use. When I need them I just take what I need and finish with sauce and cheese.

OMG!  5 stars because it was soooooo easy and soooo good!  I actually think I will make it for my super bowl party because it's so easy.  I bought the Costco rotisserie chicken and we had some leftovers. I had a container of salsa.I had the cream cheese.  I bought corn tortillas, and a can of refried beans and for some reason I thought I needed enchilada sauce. I purchased the milld "Hatch" green enchilada sauce.  I put some in the bottom of the pan.  I took my salsa and did what the recipe said to do.  I followed all the remainder steps and put some more enchilada sauce on top of the rolled enchiladas, then I put it in the oven for maybe 5 minutes covered. I uncovered it after the 5 minutes, splashed the cheese (mozzarella because that was what I had!), put it back in oven for about 3 minutes uncovered,  and with all these oops, it was fabulous!  Definitely sent the recipe to my friends and kids with families.  This is an easy recipe that is a winner!

text:
Loved how easy this was to pull together. I subbed black beans for the pinto because I didn't have any pinto beans. I also added a small can of corn in order to stretch this into more enchiladas.  For the chicken, I used canned chicken breast.  I followed past reviewers who suggested using only 1/2 the cream cheese.  I also opted for lite cream cheese to cut back on some calories.  Added about 1 tablespoon of taco seasoning mix to give it a little more flavor.  In order to Spice it up even more I added Hot jalapeno chilis diced.  I did NOT use flour tortillas ONLY because authentic enchiladas use CORN not FLOUR.  I did include some enchilada sauce as well.  I didn't want them to dry out.  Overall very easy and tasty.  EXCELLENT dish to make ahead of time and Freeze and then pop in the oven whilst still frozen.  Thanks IANKRIS !!

text:
I have been making enchaladas simmalar to these for years now, they are always a big hit with my husband, and now our kids. I use corn tortillas and flour, depending on what i have on hand, i also use pace salsa and leave out the beans sometimes. I also pour a can of enchalada sauce over them and then the cheese. I have also used this as a chip dip. And i have used it as a layer in a mexican style lasagna. (just start by layering meat sauce, refried beans and corn, then a corn tortilla.) 
TIP: if you are having trouble rolling the corn tortillas, place them in a plastic sandwich bag and seal lightly, put in the mircowave for 30 seconds this heats them enough to make them plyable and should not rip. Or you can put them a skillet of hot oil and lightly fry them on each side for 10 seconds. I will make this again.

text:
Easy, excellent recipe. I substituted a can of fat-free refried beans and 2/3 cup salsa for the cream cheese and pinto beans, and added about 1/4 cup shredded cheese to make it creamy when melted. Made one enchilada for my vegetarian daughter before adding the chicken for everyone else. Used half a can of enchilada sauce in the bottom of the dish, then poured the rest over the enchiladas once they went in. Toppings I had ready on the side: sour cream, salsa, chopped fresh tomato, sliced black olives, chopped green onions and fresh guacamole made from one of the many recipes on this site. Everyone enjoyed it. It's the first time I've made enchiladas, but it won't be the last! Thanks for the recipe. :)

text:
So Easy and So Delicious! This was almost too simple for me, so I added a few more ingredients to kick up the flavor. I cooked up my chicken to shred it finely. While it was cooking I added enchilada sauce, enchilada seasoning, sauted onions, tomato sauce, and cumin powder. To the tortilla rolls, I added a dollup of salsa, refried beans (instead of pinto beans), and shredded cheese. I topped it off with the remaining shredded cheese, salsa, and sour cream. Yes, I know I made a simple dish complex, but that is the beauty of this recipe it really allows you to add your own personal touch. :-) NOTE: The cream cheese mix is wonderful and adds a nice richness to the chicken filling.

text:
I used previous reviews, and my own imagination, to embellish on this recipe: I used the breasts, legs and thigh meat from a whole boiled chicken, which I shredded (I ended up with apx. 4 cups of chicken), then took a cup of the broth and mixed in a pkg. of fajita seasoning, poured it over the shredded chicken and let it marinade in the fridge for an hour. I used a can of Mexicorn, apx. 3 cups salsa, 6 oz. cream cheese, a can of black beans, & all the marinated chicken in the mixture. I had a big bag of 6" corn tortillas which were cracked in places, so instead of rolling up my enchiladas, I poured a little enchilada sauce into the bottom of two 9x13 pans (I had a lot of filling), then double-lined them with the tortillas, so that they curled up the sides of the pans. I poured the mixture evenly into both pans, spread strips of whole green chiles over the top of the filling, then put another layer (6 for each pan) of tortillas over the top of that. I spread the rest of a lg. can of enchilada sauce evenly over everything, covered both with foil, and baked them for apx. 30 min.. I then added 2-3 cups shredded Mexican Cheese, dotted the top w/ sliced jalapenos, and sprinkled cilantro over that. I put them back in the oven, uncovered, for 10 more min.. Finally, I browned the cheese under the broiler, cut into rectangles, and served w/ sour cream. It got rave review from my family, and I still have lots of leftovers!

text:
This makes a good vegetarian dish if you leave out the chicken, but I like using this recipe the night after we have a roast chicken to use up the leftovers.  It certainly would be easy enough to grill up some chicken breasts, use pre-packaged cooked chicken or one of those warm cooked roasters all the grocery stores seem to have now. You can make it as hot or as mild as you like by changing the "heat" of the salsa you use. I don't think this is really "company worthy", but a definite family meal keeper!

My boyfriend loved these enchiladas. I had to make a few modifications based on what I had in the pantry. I baked a chicken the night before, so I used the meat we had left over and it was a PERFECT use of leftovers. I also used black beans instead of pinto beans and 1/2 canned chopped tomatoes with green chili peppers added in addition to 1/2 cup salsa (my boyfriend is afraid of anything spicy and our hot sauce was too spicy to use alone). Like many of the other comments, I used half the cream cheese to be on the safe side. 

A big difference was omitting the cheese and I made a really simple sour cream sauce and baked the enchiladas smothered in the sauce and finished the dish with a nice sprinkle of paprika as garnish. 

Thank you for giving me a fun recipe to play with!

This was a great starter recipe!!! I love enchiladas... and always wanted to make my own....I followed a lot of the other rater suggestions.... I used black beans instead of pinto also I put some shredded mexican cheese in with the salsa and cream cheese mixture... and a can of green chiles and some taco seasoning mix....I used Drew's organic Salsa medium which was excellent and cut back the cream cheese to 4oz... I used whole wheat tortillas and a can of Enchilada sauce.... poured some sauce on the bottom and before I put the remainder of the cheeses on the top....and baked about 35 mins.... 
I served these with the Catina Pinto Beans also found on this site which I prepared in the crockpot and rice.....
My family just loved this dinner they said it was just as good as if we went out for this in a Mexican Restaurant..!! I had some leftover and my husband asked me to make him a plate for the next day for his lunch!!! I think I may try this without the beans the next time I make it and add some extra onions with the chicken and cheese mixture..... thanx so much for posting this I never would of thought this was soooo  easy to make!!!

I had wanted to make a different enchilada recipe but forgot to buy the can a soup so I ended up making these with some changes.  I reduced the cream cheese to 5oz, threw in a can of green chilies and substituted a sauted onion for the pinto beans. I would definitely make these again but next time I'd include the pinto beans!

This will be added to the monthly menu for sure.

text:
Not that this recipe needs the 911th review but here goes.  I have made this dozens of times..the first 2 times EXACTLY as written and the enchiladas were very good, but some of the tortillas dried out on the edges and the 8oz of cream overwhelmed the taste of chicken. Yet they were very tasty, good enough to be tinkered with to make it just a touch better. That's why a 4 star rating. 
The changes I made many similar to other reviewers: used 4oz of cream cheese, extra chicken (we do like meat), added small can Mexican corn, 1 can thoroughly rinsed black beans, red enchilada sauce both on the bottom of the pain, as well as on top of the tortillas. Cook covered; add cheese the last 
10 minutes leave uncovered. Served with shredded lettuce, tomatoes, sour cream, guacamole, and salsa, and sliced black olives on the side. Scrumptious!!!!

text:
This is such a great recipe!  I've made it four times in the last few months as my family requests it and it's so easy and affordable.  I'm sure the recipe is awesome as is but I make some minor mods based on my preferences:

I use rotisserie chicken and I love the flavor of enchilada sauce so I use that instead of salsa. 

I use a 10 ounce can of the enchilada sauce in with the cream cheese (I use only half a block and it's still plenty rich) and I throw about a half cup of the shredded cheese in there too.  I put about two thirds of the sauce mixture into the chicken and beans for the filling.   

I pour another half can of straight enchilada sauce  into the bottom of the casserole dish and lay each tortilla shell in the bottom of the dish as I build/fill them so the tortillas get coated in the sauce.  I top them with the remaining cheesy sauce mixture and then pile on the rest of the shredded cheese.  Half way through cooking, I drizzle the remaining half can of straight enchilada  sauce on top, finish cooking and then top with chopped green onions.   

I have also made this vegetarian, using just pinto beans,  finely diced onion and the cheesy sauce mixture for the filling.  It's great!

text:
This is a great recipe as is, or as a starting base! I decided to make with ground beef since we had chicken the night before. Ive got a household of hungry males, and they love leftovers or a frozen meal to heat up when Im not home, so I tripled the recipe. Ive kind of spoiled my family with my cooking so I knew this would be too basic for them, so I added to it. Since I knew 3x the cream cheese would be too much for them, I only did 2x but got 3 just in case. *Remember, you can always adjust recipes to your liking!* MY TWIST: 1) Cooked the 3 lbs of 82/19% beef and seasoned with a little pink Himalayan salt. Drained and left in sink. 2) Wiped down same pan, cooked 2 of 8 oz cream cheese, 4 cups Pace Picante medium salsa, 4 oz green jalapeos, 7 oz diced green chiles, and 2 of 2.25 sliced black olives. 3) In another strainer I drained 30 oz black beans, 15 oz pinto beans, and 15.25 oz crisp sweet corn. 4) Once cream cheese was fully melted, I added the ground beef, beans and corn. Stir well. This is where you can decide if you need to add more salsa or cream cheese. 5) I blended two cups of salsa in electric blender. Or, you can just use enchiladas sauce. 6) Put 1/2 blended salsa at bottom of 8x8 and 9x13 pan. 6) Made the enchiladas fat and happy! Leaving about 1 1/2 cup meat sauce aside. 7) 9x13 I put 8 in a row with 2 on side, 8x8 4 in a row with 1 on the side. 8) Add the saved meat sauce on top, then cheese then sprinkle blended salsa. 9) Cover n bake!

text:
These were really yummy but I doctored the base recipe up a bit and made this into a casserole. 
I used medium salsa and added a can of drained black beans and a can of drained green chiles/tomatoes to the salsa/cream cheese mixture.  I chopped the chicken up a bit and after I added it to the sauce mix, I stirred in taco seasoning mix-about 1/2 to  2/3 (to taste) of an envelope.  I cooked two Uncle Bens Spanish rice  containers and put the Spanish rice  in a 13 x 9 pan. I spooned a couple of ladles of enchilada sauce over it and mixed it up a bit. I then filled the tortillas and put them on top. I got 8 in the pan. I ladled a little more enchilada sauce on each enchilada  then topped it with shredded Mexican cheese. I baked it for about 40 min since I added the rice layer on the bottom.  The chicken mixture  made two 13 x9 pans. Delicious!!

text:
Came out so good! I doubled the recipe so I could have plenty of left overs. However I halved the cream cheese like several others have suggested. I also used spicy enchilada sauce (from the can) to cover the bottom of the baking dishes and also to drizzle on top of the enchiladas before layering with the cheese.  The flavor was amazing! Ate it with a side of shredded lettuce, diced tomatoes, sour cream, and some Spanish rice. Definitely hit the spot since I was craving Mexican food! And super easy to make. Will definitely make this again. (P.S. this recipe never said how to cook the chicken so I poached 3 chicken breasts in chicken broth for about 20 minutes at low heat and they came out moist and were easy to shred/chop for this recipe).

text:
My family loves this recipe! I've made it a couple different ways now. 1st time was the base recipe except I spiced it up a bit more and added some peppers, onions, black beans and a little hot sauce. I also only had medium cheddar and a little mozza cheese so I just used that in a pinch. Didn't have quite enough cream cheese in my fridge but that was fine too, still tasted amazing! I couldn't stop eating the filling as I rolled them, lol (used burrito wraps because that's all I had, worked fine just cut them in half after baking so they're easier to serve). Second time I bought a family size bag of Bird's Eye fajita dinner and cooked it as the package said and then added a can each of corn, black and pinto beans, a little salsa and the cream cheese. Used shredded mexican cheese blend from kroger and whole wheat taco tortillas. Last but not least after it was baked I ripped up some fresh cilantro on top of everything, it was SO GOOD! Such an easy, yummy and pretty quick meal that you can change up as much as you want! Love it!

I have made this many times now, but alas I did make a few changes. (I know I hate it when people do that, but I read some reviews and these made sense.) 
I added 1 can of Rotel  to the cream cheese. To the chicken I added a dash of pepper, a couple splashes of Frank's sauce,  diced jalapenos instead of chilies, and a handful of mozzarella.  No beans (No one wanted).  I then used corn tortillas, and placed 1/4 can of enchilada sauce on the bottom of pan, then topped the rolled tortillas with the other 3/4 of the can before topping with cheese and baking.  Even people who say they hated enchiladas were eating them.  They come out great every time.

Super easy and flavorful. I modified it slightly because of ingredients on hand: I mixed softened cream cheese with canned spicy tomatoes and added Hatch jalapenos (frozen from Trader Joe's). I only mixed these in a bowl. Nor did  I add the chicken or beans to the cream cheese filling but kept these items separate for layering.  Additionally I used Hatch's green enchilada sauce and added it to the shredded chicken to ensure juiciness and flavor. Instead of rolling enchiladas, I layered the ingredients: corn tortillas (not cooked), Hatch green enchilada sauce, refried beans, the cream cheese mixture, shredded chicken topped with more enchilada sauce, repeat. It made 2 full layers.  I didn't use any shredded cheese and it was moist and amazing. Baked it for 25 minutes and hubby is asking for it again. We both loved it!

text:
This is one of my favorite recipes on this site! They are delicious as written but I have experimented with minor changes and seasoned to taste. They are equally delicious with either flour or corn tortillas and it's great to have that gluten free option for certain guests. I like to shred the cooked chicken with forks instead having chopped chunks in my tortillas. I also spread the bottom of the baking dish with red enchilada sauce before placing the tortillas in it and then drizzle more sauce on top with extra cheese. It keeps it more moist. And I dice spinach leaves and add it to the filling. When doubling the recipe, I like to add one can black beans and one can of the pinto beans. These are delicious any way you choose!

text:
Nice, easy way to make enchiladas. I did change a few things. One, I used corn tortillas. Two, I cooked my chicken breasts in the slow cooker, seasoned with cumin, garlic, chili powder, pepper, and a some green chili sauce. I shredded the chicken after about four hours, cooked two hours more on low. I used low fat cream cheese, another can of green enchilada sauce. I mixed them together, with a few more of the same spices I used on the chicken.  I didn't add the beans to the enchilada, I just put them on the side. Very delicious!

text:
I sliced the chicken breast into thin pieces and sauted it with some southwest seasoning then removed the chicken from the skillet.  I substituted enchilada sauce for the salsa and cut the cream cheese up into pieces to help it melt.  I added the chicken and beans to the mixture and put it inside corn tortillas.  As mentioned previously I put a little enchilada sauce in the baking dish before adding the stuffed tortillas then poured some more enchilada sauce over the entire batch and bake loosely covered for 25 minutes adding the cheddar jack cheese to bake for an additional 5 minutes.

Excellent base recipe. I made a few tweaks though. I used black beans instead of pinto, added green chiles as recommended in other reviews, added yellow rice, poured enchilada sauce on and put the cheese on halfway through baking, and use corn tortillas instead of flour to give it a more authentic taste. text:
I saw this recipe and I thought I have to try this. However, I did make a few adjustment as recommended by a couple of other reviewers:
1) I used about 5 ozs  of cream cheese, instead of the full 8 ozs. 
2) Omitted the pinto beans
3) Used corn tortillas instead of flour
4) Used 1/2 cup salsa and 1/2 cup enchilada sauce (instead of 1cup of only salsa)
5) poured a layer of enchilada sauce in bottom of baking dish before placing in enchiladas
Also for convenience, I  decided to use Oscar Myer precooked Southwest Chicken Strips mixed with a can of Tyson Grilled Premium Chicken. My family and I loved this dish. I think the recommendation of corn tortillas really made it taste a little more authentic. This dish will definitely be added to my dinner rotation menu. Simple, quick and delicious!

text:
These came out delicious.  I did not have packaged tortillas, so I made homemade ones, which added a fresh taste I think.  Also, did not have salsa, so used enchilada sauce mixed with a little chili sauce, and had no pinto beans, so used fava beans--still came out well.  I also put some enchilada sauce on the bottom of the casserole dish as suggested, and before putting cheese over entree, covered with some enchilada sauce.  I used a tip someone gave me and sprayed the Reynolds wrap with Pam so the cheese would not stick to wrap while baking.  When I make again, will still use enchilada sauce vs. salsa, as I am not a big fan of salsa, but would like to use pinto beans--although the fava beans turned out to be a good substitute.

text:
My husband's favorite meal is enchiladas, so I wanted to try making them for the first time.  He said that these were better than his mom's! I cut the cream cheese in half to 4oz and added half a can of diced green chiles.  I used low fat cream cheese and lowfat shredded Mexican cheese - it was very good that way and doesn't need the full-fat cheese.  2cups of cheese is a lot - I will go down to 1.5 cups next time.  I used precooked end chicken breasts from the grocery store deli counter.  They were big chicken breasts and I used 1.5 of them to make 8 enchiladas.  I also used a can of enchilada sauce.  I sprayed the bottom of the pan with olive oil, then coated it with a little enchilada sauce - put the enchiladas in, and then coated them well with the rest of the enchilada sauce.  I baked for 15 minutes with the foil in, then added the cheese and baked for 10 min with the foil on, then baked for 5 minutes with foil off.  Served with sour cream on top.

This was really good and so easy to make.  After reading the reviews, I made the following changes.  1.  used 4 oz of low fat cream cheese.  2.  used 1/2 jar salsa in the heated mixture and reserved  1/2 for the bottom of casserole dish and to top the enchilada's off (to avoid them drying out or hardening).  3.  added cooked corn from 1 ear.  4.  added canned chili peppers.  5.  added cilantro.  6. used Costco rotisserie chicken.  7. Trader Joe's lite mexican blend cheese.  The only thing I would do differently next time is to add some heat with jalapeo's.

text:
The recipe serves six and calls for 6 six-inch tortillas, but it took 13 tortillas to fill. Not sure what happened (maybe the 7 loaves/7 fishes syndrome kicked in). I would suggest that you remove the chicken filling from the heat and let cool a few minutes before filling the tortilla bread (or else Yowch). Another suggestion: Your choice of salsa will MAKE or BREAK this recipe. Get a good salsa (and pay more than a dollar for it)! I used a locally made chipotle salsa (and paid $6 for the jar). I also used a red chile enchilada sauce to keep the outside colorful and flavorful. I served my enchiladas with rice and a green garden salad consisting of romaine lettuce, pico de gallo, and black olives. An easy and quick to put together recipe that made a tasty dinner!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Easy and basic--many people will want to add some oomph. Instead, I dip flour tortillas into enchilada sauce, and then make a basic filling of 1/2 pkg cream cheese and 1/2 pt of sour cream (melted on the stove together so I can really mix them), and mix that with 2 cups of shredded chicken. Put the filling into the dipped tortillas. That's the basic, delicious but bland start. Then everyone can add a spoonfull of their favorite toppings before rolling the enchiladas. Add guacamole, or salsa, or chilies to add a bit of zip. If you want even more flavor, you can add a bit of seasoning to the cream cheese/sour cream mix. Roll the enchiladas and place in a baking dish seam side down, top with some shredded colby jack or pepper jack cheese, cover in foil or a lid, and bake at 325 for 25 mins. SOoo good and it's a great recipe where everyone can customize their own jut a bit.

text:
Meh. These were just so-so. The consensus at our dinner table was unanimous - myself, my husband and our dinner guest (our neighbor) all agreed that while tasty, these were too dry for our liking. The filling itself is SUPER yummy (and I even used a generic (Wal-Mart) brand salsa), but the enchiladas themselves need some "help." A simple sauce would make all the difference, IMHO. If I ever make these again, I'll definitely keep this in mind. Cilantro, onion, tomato, lettuce and a dab of sour cream were yummy garnishes. Corn, Mexican rice and margaritas completed our meal. If for nothing else, this will become one of those "save the day" go-to recipes I rely upon when my pantry is bare and I have little time to prepare dinner. Thanks anyways, IANKRIS. :-)

text:
The recipe was great and is super easy - just my style. I also use enchilada sauce instead of salsa. The first time I made it, I personally thought the sauce was too creamy, so, I use half the cream cheese (1/3 fat, too). It really very good. My husband loved it and asked for it again! A+
***UPDATE*** Regularly Make this and have passed the recipe along to another who's family absolutely loved it!!! One Good Idea: I have made this ahead and stored it in the fridge, then it is ready to just be "popped in" the oven for an even faster supper!! I also prefer using fat free refried beans instead of regular pinto. Spread  the mixture in each tortillas, THEN fill the them with the cheese/chicken/enchilda mixture -  holds the enchildas together better.
